Japanese Army, Navy, and Foreign Ministries Decide on Diplomatic Policy 47

Based on the Monroe Doctrine of East Asia - Improving Sino-Japanese Relations and Joint Anti-Communism

Tokyo - The fundamental policy of Japanese diplomacy after withdrawing from the arms reduction conference has been clearly expressed in Foreign Minister Hirota's speech on diplomatic policy at the 68th Diet session. In order to adjust the details and specific plans for implementation, the three ministries of the Army, Navy, and Foreign Affairs have been holding liaison meetings for days, and the deliberations have been extremely cautious. It is confirmed that the main proposals on which the three ministries have reached complete agreement are as follows:

The era of the Navy becoming unconditional is not something that can be obtained by seeking it. Therefore, Japan should try its best to avoid causing the predictable free competition in shipbuilding in the absence of treaties.

The relationship between China and Japan depends on China's recognition of the existence of "Manchukuo." Improvement can be gradually achieved. Sino-Japanese cooperation and joint defense against communism are indispensable requirements for Japan to implement its East Asian policy. It is always necessary to move towards the path of realization as soon as possible.

Japan believes that the true intentions of the naval issue and the China issue can be gradually understood by various countries. It promises the United Kingdom and the United States to request freedom of commerce in order to remove the causes that threaten peace.

The Far East Red Army is a constant threat to "Manchukuo." The Soviet Union's communist activities are a fundamental obstacle to Japan's East Asian policy. Therefore, the demarcation of the Manchurian-Soviet border, the withdrawal of the Far East Red Army, and the completion of the joint defense against communism by Japan and China will prevent the occurrence of unfortunate events between Japan and the Soviet Union. This is what we firmly believe. The above-mentioned Japanese foreign policy is based on the principle of non-threat and non-aggression. It is due to the natural expansion of the leaping Japan, which spreads it to the four seas by peaceful means. Therefore, no country in the world is allowed to carry out illegal advances. East Asia is considered to be East Asia for East Asians, and it is gradually used to establish permanent world peace. (Allied News Agency dispatch on the 7th)

Tokyo - Yesterday, in order to deal with the Manchurian-Soviet and Manchurian-Mongolian border disputes and to determine the policy toward the Soviet Union, a three-ministry council of the Army, Navy, and Foreign Affairs was held at the Ministry of Foreign Affairs on the 6th. As a result of the discussion, quite strong opinions were present. As for the incidents of clashes between Japanese and Soviet soldiers, the Foreign Affairs authorities will judge the right and wrong after the situation becomes clear, or protest to the Soviet government or call attention to it next week. These opinions have been agreed upon and are recorded below:

The Japanese government, based on the policy of good neighborliness, non-threat, and non-aggression, strives to maintain peaceful and friendly relations with the Soviet Union and seeks to promote goodwill.

Based on the above principles, it is believed that the fundamental solution to border disputes is to first demarcate the unclear border. If the Soviet government hopes to seek means and methods to deal with disputes, then it is harmless for both parties to begin consultations.

As for the instability on the border, it is caused by the Soviet Union's expansion of unnecessary and huge military equipment. It goes without saying that the Soviet Union should be urged to reflect on this.

The above points are the adjustments to the attitude toward relations with the Soviet Union that have been established. Although the words and actions of the Soviet Union are stimulating, their hearts are extremely afraid of Japan's counterattack. Soviet Ambassador to Japan Yurenev proposed to Japan on August 17 last year to establish a border dispute handling committee, and he has repeatedly raised it whenever there is an opportunity. This shows that the director of the European and Asian Affairs Bureau, Togo, reported the progress to Chongguang after the council, and studied the specific countermeasure for the negotiation with the Soviet Union. In the end, regarding the conflict incidents, Ambassador Ota will protest to the Soviet government and explain Japan's policy for eradicating disputes and ask it to reflect on it. The second step in adjusting the border dispute issue will be to continue the negotiations that were suspended last year in Tokyo by Foreign Minister Hirota and Ambassador Yurenev. (Allied News Agency dispatch on the 7th)

Isogai Argues That Various Issues in North China Must Be Resolved Separately 48

Tokyo - The Yomiuri Shimbun reported that when the General Staff personnel gathered yesterday, Major General Isogai, the military attache of the Japanese Embassy in China, stipulated the following principles: All issues related to North China must be dealt with separately and must not be discussed in the Sino-Japanese conferences held in Nanjing. (Reuters dispatch on the 7th)

British Merchants Suffer Losses Due to Petroleum Monopoly, Requesting Compensation from the Puppet Government 49

London - The British Parliament focused on diplomatic issues on the 6th. Among the questions about the recent situation in the Far East, the current situation in "Manchukuo" and the interests of the United Kingdom, one member of parliament asked what countermeasures the government would take regarding the losses suffered by British merchants as a result of the "Manchukuo" monopoly of petroleum. The answer from the Under-Secretary of State for Foreign Affairs, Mr. Flandrin, was as follows:

The British rights and interests have suffered losses due to the "Manchukuo" determination of the petroleum monopoly system. Regarding the issue of compensation, negotiations are currently being conducted between the merchants concerned and the "Manchukuo" government. However, no agreement has been reached on the amount of compensation and other specific matters. The government hopes that the agreement will be established as soon as possible and is willing to fully exert its mediation efforts. (Allied News Agency dispatch on the 6th)

American Navy Proposes Large-Scale Renovation of the Navy 50

Mr. Vincent Submits Four Proposals to the House - Stipulating the Construction of 221,000 Tons of Auxiliary Ships

Washington - Mr. Vincent, chairman of the House Naval Affairs Committee, proposed to the House today to expand the US Navy by eight battleships. The third proposal suggests abolishing outdated battleships. The fourth proposal requests an appropriation of six million yuan to continue building twelve battleships. (National Telegram dispatch on the 6th)

Washington - Mr. Vincent, chairman of the House Naval Affairs Committee and a Democrat, today submitted three bills to the House, all stipulating the procedures for large-scale naval renovation, including the construction of 221,000 tons of auxiliary ships. All three bills have received the support of the Navy Department. According to one of the four bills proposed by Senator Tramell, chairman of the Senate Naval Affairs Committee, in the House on February 4, it also stipulates the construction of 221,000 tons of auxiliary ships. (Reuters dispatch on the 6th)

US Builds Air Force Bases - Exceeding the Scope of National Defense Needs 51

Washington - Senior officials believe that the Wilcox Bill, which advocates building strong military aviation bases in important locations on the US border and overseas territories, has failed. According to the report prepared by the Special Military Committee, it was submitted to Secretary of War Dern today. Because it belongs to national defense secrets, it will never be published. This report, in addition to being used as a reference for future national defense arrangements, is unlikely to be used for other purposes. Observers believe that building air force bases will exceed the scope of current national defense needs. Senior military officers also believe that it is unlikely that these very costly bases will be built domestically, but there may be a need for them at sea. In short, the general public believes that it is better to build aircraft than to build aircraft bases with useful money. (National Telegram dispatch on the 6th)

Renovating Eight Navy Shipyards - Estimated to Cost 20 Million Yuan 52

Washington - The Senate Munitions Investigating Committee learned today that if eight navy shipyards are to be renovated so that the government can build all of its own battleships, it will require an expenditure of 23 million yuan. This amount was submitted by the State Commercial Federation at the request of the Senate Committee. The committee also estimated that the government builds 17 battleships annually, costing 150 million yuan. By this analogy, twenty years later, it can build 20 battleships, 20 aircraft carriers, 20 heavy cruisers, 20 light cruisers, 200 destroyers, and 45 submarines. As for the cost of the government manufacturing all military equipment, if it wants to double the output of Colt Company's machine guns and small guns, it will cost 8 million yuan. Doubling the output of Brewerd Company's aircraft will cost 11 million yuan. Doubling the output of DuPont Company's military supplies will cost 3 million yuan. (National Telegram dispatch on the 6th)

Japanese Ships Cruise Alaska - Overtly Fishing, Covertly Measuring Terrain 53

Washington - Mr. Sirovich, a Democratic representative from New York, stated before the House Merchant Marine Committee today that many Japanese ships cruise off the coast of Alaska, ostensibly fishing, but actually engaging in military operations. These Japanese ships are measuring water depths, taking photographs of the coastline terrain, and checking where aircraft can land and where submarines can be based. Japan's purpose is to seize Alaska once war breaks out in order to obtain a food source for its people, because the Japanese live on fish. (Reuters dispatch on the 6th)

Tokyo - When the House Merchant Marine Committee of the United States gathered, Sirovich claimed that Japanese people in Alaska outwardly engaged in fishing, but in reality had military purposes, measuring water depth, taking photographs of the coastline terrain, and looking for locations for future airfields and submarine bases, in order to seize Alaska in the event of war, etc. Spokespersons for the Japanese Foreign Ministry and Navy Ministry today rejected this statement as too absurd and not worth criticizing. The Foreign Ministry spokesperson also said that this is a test of the level of education and knowledge of Americans and whether they are easily gullible. (Reuters dispatch on the 7th)

Main Battleship Tonnage Issue: Four Nations Find Compromise Unlikely 54

London: Admiral Raineri, the Italian representative at the Naval Conference, today visited Lieutenant General Robert, the French representative, to discuss the issue of main battleship tonnage and the future prospects of the Naval Conference. According to our correspondent, France and Italy hold completely identical views on the main battleship tonnage issue, advocating a maximum limit of 27,000 or 28,000 tons. At present, the main battleship tonnage issue remains a major obstacle to the establishment of a four-nation agreement. It is still unknown whether the expert subcommittee will raise this issue for discussion at its meeting tomorrow morning at Clarence House, as the subcommittee will first review the report submitted by the members of the committee responsible for studying the definition of warships. This committee continued its work this afternoon and has already decided on the following measures: Adopting the American proposal to increase the age of main battleships from twenty years to twenty-six years; Setting the age of cruisers at twenty years; Setting the age of destroyers at sixteen years; Setting the age of submarines at thirteen years; Any warship with a tonnage of 10,000 tons or more and a cannon caliber of eight inches or more shall be considered a main battleship; The definition of displacement shall still adopt the definition contained in the Washington Naval Treaty, that is, the displacement after the completion of construction, complete equipment, and complete navigation equipment; Small warships, such as shallow water coastal defense ships, are originally not subject to qualitative restrictions, and their construction does not need to be notified to each other. In the future, although they are still not subject to qualitative restrictions, they should be included in the annual warship construction program and notified to each other. (Havas dispatch, 6th)

New British Naval Commander to China Arrives in the Philippines on a Cruiser 55

Manila: The British cruiser HMS Kent, carrying Sir Reginald Henderson, the commander of the British China Station fleet, arrived here this morning. Due to the death of the British monarch, there were no public welcoming ceremonies. (Reuters dispatch, 7th)

British Military Aircraft Visit Japan; Japan Prepares to Welcome Them 56

First Phase of Paris Diplomatic Talks Ends; Austrian Vice-Chancellor and Russian Foreign Minister Return Home; Czech Premier Sets Out for Paris 57

Paris: The first phase of the diplomatic talks held in Paris has now come to an end. Prince Paul, the Regent of Yugoslavia, held a grand banquet today for French cabinet members and political figures. The second phase of the talks will begin when the Czech Prime Minister arrives here. The King of Denmark arrived here today, but it is generally believed that this trip has no political significance. (National Telegram, 6th)

Paris: Turkish Foreign Minister Rüştü, who participated in the Paris diplomatic talks, told reporters from the Paris newspaper today that the Paris diplomatic talks had no real results. He further said that this must be the purpose of the talks. The purpose of the talks was to study collective security and discuss Article 16 of the Covenant of the League of Nations. There have been two tests of collective security: the first is economic sanctions and the concentration of the British Navy in the Mediterranean; the second is the British solicitation of opinions from various countries on what attitude each country will take in the event of war. Therefore, from this point of view, collective security can be said to be quite successful. The ominous clouds over the Mediterranean three months ago have now subsided. (National Telegram, 6th)

Czech Capital: Premier Hodža has decided to go to Paris on the 8th of this month to discuss the international situation. He told our correspondent that "Among the issues in Central Europe that need to be resolved urgently is the issue of the relationship between the countries of the Little Entente and the countries that signed the Rome Accords (signed in March 1934), that is, Italy, Austria, and Hungary. Since Austrian Chancellor Schuschnigg came here to visit, the Czech Republic and Austria have been able to understand each other better than in the past, and a trade agreement between the two countries will soon be concluded." Hodža also said that he would go to Yugoslavia on his way back from Paris, but a trip to Romania seemed unnecessary, as he would meet with Romanian Foreign Minister Titulescu in Paris. (Havas dispatch, 7th)

Soviet Russia and Romania Negotiate a Military Treaty: Nature Similar to French-Russian and Russian-Czech Mutual Assistance Treaties; Negotiations Proceed Smoothly 58

London: The Soviet Union and Romania are currently negotiating a military treaty (as reported in yesterday's telegram, which is about to be signed). According to people from the Little Entente, the content of this treaty is roughly the same as the French-Russian and Russian-Czech mutual assistance treaties, and stipulates that if war breaks out between Hungary and Romania, the Soviet Union should automatically send troops to assist. One of the most difficult points in the negotiations between Russia and Romania is the issue of the passage of Russian troops, that is, if Czechoslovakia is invaded by Germany, the Soviet Union should send troops to assist according to the Russian-Czech mutual assistance treaty. At that time, Romania should allow the passage of Soviet land and air forces to help Czechoslovakia. The discussion of this issue took a lot of effort. Later, because the Russian treaty is based on Article 16 of the League of Nations Covenant, if Czechoslovakia is invaded by Germany, both Russia and Romania are member states of the League of Nations and have an obligation to assist Czechoslovakia. The passage of troops is naturally not a problem and does not need to be stipulated in the Russian treaty. Therefore, this difficulty was resolved. In addition, the issue of sovereignty over Bessarabia (which belonged to Russia before the war and is now owned by Romania) was definitively resolved during the London Economic Conference in 1933 when Russia, Poland, and eight other countries signed the definition of aggressor. Therefore, if Soviet troops pass through the province, it will not cause incidents. The current negotiations between Russia and Romania have a long history. They almost succeeded when Romanian Foreign Minister Titulescu visited London in early July last year, but were suspended due to Yugoslavia's doubts about the Soviet Union's intentions. Now, Russia and Romania are on good terms, so the negotiations can proceed smoothly. (Havas dispatch, 6th)

France Negotiates Loan from Britain; Progress Made in Negotiations 59

London: According to financial circles here, progress has been made in the negotiations between France and Britain regarding a loan from Britain. Both parties agree that after the loan is completed, it will not be done by means of remittance (referring to the remittance of pounds to France), and the British Exchange Equalisation Account will also not formally and directly participate in the matter, so that it will not be necessary to request the approval of Parliament. Generally speaking, Britain will lend pounds to France, and France will exchange francs for pounds on the London market and then remit them to Paris. After these pounds are sold on the London market, the foreign exchange market will inevitably fall. At that time, the Equalisation Account will find ways to remedy it. According to financial circles, after the loan is completed, the Bank of France will not increase the issuance of banknotes. (Havas dispatch, 6th)

Page 8

North Road Front: Abyssinian Army Victory Verified; High Morale; Capture of Makaleh Imminent; Guerrilla Warfare Used to Wear Down the Enemy 60

Taixi: Dr. Piero Raffaelli, a member of the Irish Ambulance Unit, arrived here today and verified the Abyssinian claim that the Abyssinian army had won a major victory over the Italian army in the Danakil region. Dr. Raffaelli worked in the ambulance unit three miles from Magale. He traveled by mule for fifteen days to reach here. He is the first white man to return here from the North Road front. Dr. Raffaelli described in detail the difficulties of the ambulance unit members' work and said that everyone was well, but they needed everything. They have not received mail in the past two days. There is currently no tobacco or salt, and working under high air pressure, they treat an average of 100 seriously wounded soldiers every day. He also said that Italian planes bomb the ambulance unit's tents with machine guns and bombs almost every day. (Reuters dispatch, 6th)

Abyssinian Capital: Our special correspondent, Ochsner, reports that a certain European gentleman who had previously left with the army and stayed in the first line of defense of Magaleh on the North Road for many days is familiar with the situation at the front. According to his observations, the Abyssinian army clearly has the upper hand on the Tigray Province front on the North Road, and its morale is higher than that of the Italian army. However, at present, the Abyssinian army does not want to extend the lines of communication, which is unfavorable. Therefore, it is determined to hold the existing lines of defense and not advance further, but only adopt guerrilla tactics to wear down the enemy. They often sneak through the barbed wire at night and launch attacks on small Italian army camps. During the day, they only launch surprise attacks on Italian army supply convoys and outposts. As a result, the Italian army is in great distress and has suffered considerable losses. The positions abandoned by the Italian army are occupied by the Abyssinian army. The European gentleman believes that the Abyssinian army will soon be able to recapture Magaleh by adopting this tactic. Once Magaleh falls, the Abyssinian army will seize the opportunity to advance and capture Adowa. (Havas dispatch, 6th)

Italian Premier's Son-in-Law Goes to East Africa Again 61

Rome: Count Ciano, the son-in-law of Italian Premier Mussolini, set off today for Naples to go to East Africa to take up the position of Air Force Captain. At the time of departure, there were military bands and guards to see him off, and flags were hung everywhere. Fascist Party Secretary Starace accompanied him. (Reuters dispatch, 7th)

Denial of Supplying Abyssinia with Illegal Munitions 62

Geneva: The British government sent a letter to the League of Nations denying the Italian claim that British manufacturers manufactured dumdum bullets or military explosive ammunition for Abyssinia, saying that this statement was completely unfounded. In fact, the British government's control over arms exports is extremely strict, so the authorities dare to believe that British companies abide by international regulations and standards. It also said that the British government does not want to express its opinion on the Italian claim that the Abyssinian army used illegal ammunition, but Britain cannot remain silent on the Italian accusation against British manufacturers.

League of Nations Oil Embargo Against Italy: Success or Failure Depends on the United States; Expert Subcommittee Completes Report 63

Geneva: The expert subcommittee considering the issue of oil substitutes has prepared a report stating that Italy will be unable to do anything without oil imports, and Italy does not have the necessary machinery to produce sufficient oil substitutes. (Reuters dispatch, 7th)

Geneva: The committee of experts on the issue of coal oil embargo, which belongs to the League of Nations' eighteen-nation subcommittee, had previously appointed members of the committee to specialize in the issue of coal oil substitutes. The committee has now completed its work, and its report was approved by the expert committee tonight. It is said that any country that intends to use substitutes to replace coal oil can only reach a maximum ratio of 15% to 20% of the total consumption in peacetime, and it is impossible to exceed this. Therefore, if the coal oil embargo can be implemented, it will definitely have a practical effect and bring the current war to a swift end. Regarding the issue of transporting Italian coal oil and its by-products, the expert committee will meet tomorrow to study it. (Havas dispatch, 6th)

Geneva: League of Nations personnel recently declared that the eighteen-nation subcommittee is unlikely to be convened between the end of this month and the beginning of next month, because it is not yet known what decision the US Congress will make on the new Neutrality Act. The eighteen-nation committee will naturally be at a loss as to what to do about the coal oil embargo. If the US Congress decides to maintain the status quo stipulated by the current Neutrality Act in accordance with the current opinions of the members, the League of Nations' sanctions against Italy will inevitably fail, and the United States will bear the responsibility. Advocates of sanctions say that the report to be submitted by the eighteen-nation committee's expert committee on the coal oil embargo states that if the amount of coal oil exported by the United States to Italy can be reduced to the normal export amount, the League of Nations' sanctions will have a practical effect. If the US exports of coal oil to Italy are reduced to pre-war levels, Italy's needs can only be met by 5%. It is heard that US President Roosevelt can theoretically include coal oil in the list of items necessary for war in accordance with the current Neutrality Act and order it to be prohibited from being transported to belligerent countries, but due to the obstruction of the current attitude of the US Congress, it is unlikely that a decision will be made. (Havas dispatch, 7th)

New League of Nations Building Completed; Officially Moves in on the 17th of This Month 64

Old Headquarters Sold to the Swiss Government

Geneva: The League of Nations' new headquarters, the Ariana Palace, has now been completed and is scheduled to move in on the 17th of this month. Six Swiss moving companies have contracted to handle the relocation. Since the League of Nations began operating in the old headquarters in 1920, fifteen years have passed, and there are many documents and archives stored there, so the relocation procedures will take a week to complete. However, the League of Nations' library, which contains 200,000 books, and a side building built for the Disarmament Conference in 1931, will be relocated in the spring. The old headquarters was previously put up for auction and has now been purchased by the Swiss government for 4 million Swiss francs. It is said that it will be rented out to various private international organizations scattered here. (Havas dispatch, 6th)

Germany Demands Restoration of Old Colonies 66

London: Lord Londonderry, the former British Secretary of State for Air, visited the Olympic Games winter sports program in Garmisch, Germany, and is now staying in Berlin for a few days. It is heard that he informally visited German leader Hitler and his disarmament special envoy Ribbentrop, both of whom reiterated Germany's demand for the restoration of its colonies to Londonderry. Ribbentrop also said that this move was necessary because it was related to equal rights and German honor. Ribbentrop also said that Germany's rearmament was a natural result of the Soviet Union's expansion of armaments and its policies, so all Western European countries should unite to deal with the dangers of communism. According to private sources, the UK and Germany do not intend to hold negotiations on the colonial issue through diplomatic channels, but will be discussed by Lord Mount Temple, chairman of the British-German Friendship Association, and Ribbentrop. Informed sources in the British capital claim that they are unaware of the informal talks that Lord Londonderry held in Germany, and that Lord Londonderry did not have any mission when he went to Germany, so the British government is not bound by these talks. However, according to British parliamentarians, this type of talk is of a semi-official nature, and if it goes smoothly, Germany will formally demand the colonial issue. In the past, before the UK made important proposals to Germany, important British figures and German politicians would hold semi-official talks. At the beginning of last year, Liberal Party Senator Lord Lothian went to Germany on behalf of former Prime Minister MacDonald to discuss the disarmament issue. (Havas dispatch, 6th)

Sluice Workers' Petition Yields Slight Results

It is feared that it will be impossible to stop those who continue to come to Yangzhou to petition. It is not known to what extent it will evolve in the future. They requested that the government convene the merchants to study solutions, first transport the salt stored in the Gan Four fiscal year, already taxed but not processed, and the Seven Company stored salt in the sluice as soon as possible, and then report and pay the salt that should be transported by sail in the Gan Five fiscal year, in accordance with the original plan, in order to maintain the status quo and resolve disputes. Otherwise, the livelihoods of hundreds of thousands of workers will be cut off, which will not only affect social stability but also violate humanitarianism. The county government has informed the salt merchants' association and the salt affairs office on both sides of the river to handle the matter quickly, and ordered the representatives of the labor union to earnestly prevent the petitioning workers from coming to Yangzhou, but promised to send representatives to the salt affairs agency to petition. If there is any gathering of people to create disturbances, the union will be held accountable.

Gaoyou Yangzhou-Qingjiang Road Temporarily Closed for Three Months

The long-distance bus on the Yangzhou-Qingjiang Road had a major accident on January 6 in Fengshen Temple in the county, overturning into the river. Various groups in the county telegraphed the provincial government, requesting the construction of another motor road. This has been reported in this newspaper many times. It is now learned that Director Shen Baixian of the Construction Department, in view of this unfortunate incident, has not only punished those responsible and consoled the families of the deceased, but has also ordered the highway management office to temporarily close the Yangzhou-Qingjiang section for three months. All vehicles must be transported to Zhenjiang for thorough repairs. Before resuming operations, each vehicle must be carefully inspected for damage before it can be driven. The entire road surface will not only be repaired section by section, but the road surface near Shaobo will also be widened to 160 meters. The dangerous section of the Seven Public Hall in the county was originally planned to be demolished, but due to the public's adherence to customs, it was not easy to implement. It has now been decided to build a wide motor road behind the Seven Public Hall. The construction project has been approved, and the funding has been determined to be 50,000 yuan. Construction began on February 1. The construction plan has been ordered to be submitted by County Magistrate Cao of this county for approval in order to ensure the safety of vehicles.

Special Report

Biological Survey and Research Undertakings That China Urgently Needs to Conduct 93

— Hu Xiansu

A nation's resources are nothing more than two major categories: organic and inorganic. The inorganic part, such as hydropower, falls under the scope of engineering, while minerals fall under the scope of geology (although coal and petroleum are formed from organic matter, they are still considered minerals). The organic part falls under the scope of biology, including both plants and animals. The application of biology is related to all aspects of human life, including clothing, food, housing, transportation, birth, aging, illness, and death. In general, it can be divided into three categories: industry, agriculture, and medicine. Those related to industry include leather, fiber, paper, rayon, explosives, paints, and wood. Those related to agriculture include animal husbandry, fisheries, crops, horticulture, pest control, and brewing. Those related to medicine include herbal medicine, parasites, and all physiological and pathological research. Since the application of biology is so broad, it is necessary to make strong distinctions. Considering various European and American countries, research related to human health and medicine is mostly managed by health authorities; research directly related to agriculture is managed by agricultural authorities; fisheries are managed by fisheries authorities; and forestry, due to its larger scope, is managed by forestry authorities. As for insects, there are often national insect bureaus to manage them. In addition, there are many types of biological research that may not be directly applicable, but have close relationships with applications, which are often managed by specialized academic institutions, such as the Royal Botanic Gardens, Kew in England, the Bureau of Plant Industry and the Biological Survey of the United States Department of Agriculture, the National Museum, and the Institute of Applied Botany in Russia. The size of the undertaking and the importance of the powers are determined by the background of history and inheritance, without any fixed rules. However, in scientifically advanced countries, it is well known that the research of pure science may not seem to have a close relationship with applications at first glance, but very important application results are often discovered from pure scientific research, such as the discovery of plants that produce rubber substitutes in Soviet Russia, and the discovery of croton by the Zhejiang Entomological Bureau, which can be used as a very important insecticide. Usually, researchers of applied biological sciences, such as agricultural, forestry, fishery, and animal husbandry experts, often do not have in-depth studies of fundamental sciences such as zoology and botany, so they often have to seek help from purely research-oriented zoologists and botanists. Seeing this, advanced European and American countries have spared no effort in promoting biological research. For example, the Royal Botanic Gardens, Kew in England, is the largest and best-performing scientific institution in England; the Institute of Applied Botany in Russia has an annual budget of millions of rubles; and the National Biological Survey of the United States is also very large in scale. The history of biological research in our country is very short. Although there are now six or seven research institutes, and the achievements are quite excellent, the funding is extremely tight. There are many types of research that could be carried out in specialized application institutions, such as agricultural research institutes, but with everything waiting to be done, and talent and funding insufficient, it is impossible to proceed in these institutions. It is up to the country to determine what kind of biological research is most urgent for China today, whether to establish a separate institution to manage it, or to fund existing biological research institutions to undertake this work, so that the benefits can be great and fast, which can be foreseen.

Regarding the biological surveys and research undertakings that need to be carried out urgently, there are the following items:

(1) Research on forests

There are three major reasons why forestry has been promoted in our country for a long time, but the effect has not been significant: First, those who study forestry have not studied the trees of China, so there is no way to investigate what kinds of trees our country produces, and the yield, distribution, and area of various trees. Second, since the varieties of trees cannot be distinguished, the physical and chemical properties of wood cannot be studied, and all research on wood utilization cannot be started. Third, without distinguishing tree species, it is of course impossible to study the afforestation needs of various trees. Therefore, all past afforestation undertakings have been like a blind man describing an elephant. To remedy this, the following tasks must be carried out:

(A) Survey of tree species and compilation of a national tree atlas

There are extremely many kinds of trees in China. There are only more than 600 kinds of trees in North America, while in China, there are already 2,000 known kinds of trees, and new species are discovered every year. In the past four years, as many as eight new species have been discovered in a new genus. However, many more remote provinces and regions have not been explored in detail. In the past, the governments of the United States, Japan, and Annam all used great efforts to investigate tree species and compile huge and exquisite forest plant atlases. Our country should not lag behind again. Fortunately, various domestic biological research institutions have long-term collection and research. If a larger amount of money is allocated specifically for this purpose, such as the United States Department of Agriculture entrusting the Arnold Arboretum of Harvard University to compile the "North American Tree Flora," it will not be difficult to complete this great undertaking within ten years.

(B) Survey of forest area

What can be carried out at the same time as the survey of tree species is the survey of forest area. What kinds of trees are all the forests in the provinces composed of? How much area does a certain forest occupy? There has never been a large-scale survey. This kind of investigation is an urgent task. If there is this kind of survey in the whole country, when you want to use a certain kind of wood, it is not difficult to follow the map, and you can know how much its forest area is, which is enough to supply such a big market, and you can determine the development plan.

(C) Testing of material properties and identification of wood

Using wood anatomical properties to identify the types of wood is as important as surveying tree species. Since our country has been promoting afforestation for more than 30 years, no one has devoted themselves to this. This research was initiated by the Jing Sheng Biological Investigation Institute. The institute has collected wood from Hebei, Jiangxi, Sichuan, Yunnan, Guizhou, Guangdong, and Guangxi provinces, and has studied the wood anatomy of more than 400 species. Almost all genera of important softwood and hardwood have been collected, laying a rough foundation for this research. If the funding for this research can be increased and given time, the wood anatomy of all the trees in the country can be studied, and foresters and industrialists will have a guide. As for material property testing, it is necessary to purchase wood testing machines and collect large quantities of wood for testing, which is very expensive, so the Jing Sheng Biological Investigation Institute has not been able to carry out this work for the time being. However, the specific gravity of more than 400 kinds of wood has been studied. This type of research has already begun. Although other industrial research institutions have also done this research, because no one can identify tree species, it is not easy to obtain wood, so large-scale research has not been possible. If special funds are allocated to purchase wood testing machines and for large-scale collection, the foundation for all wood utilization in China can be laid, and the source of wood for industrial, military, papermaking, and railway sleepers will be known.

(D) Research on afforestation

Today's afforestation is done without testing, so the results are not good and often fail. It is appropriate to collect seeds of all important trees to study their afforestation needs, so that future afforestation practitioners will have something to follow. Today, European and American countries are promoting afforestation with hybrid poplars because they grow extremely fast. Fifteen years of growth can equal fifty years of other trees. In the future, if the suitability of the climate and soil is studied, it will not be difficult to cause a revolution in our country's forestry by using it for large-scale afforestation, and the problems of papermaking and other wood can be solved. (To be continued)

Prevention and Treatment of Infectious Diseases, Technical Expert of the National Health Administration 94

— Xu Suen

Definition: People should already have a considerable understanding of the term "infectious disease." Regarding the content of infectious diseases, if analyzed according to the nature of the disease, it can be divided into two types: direct transmission and indirect transmission. If divided by time, there is also the saying of "epidemic," which is when a certain infectious disease is most prevalent in a certain season, sometimes called "pandemic," such as influenza and epidemic cerebrospinal meningitis. There are also several infectious diseases that are often more prevalent in a certain area, and stop transmitting immediately when moved to another place. This is divided by region and is also called "endemic disease." The pathology of infectious diseases has been studied and experimented by many medical experts, and they all agree that diseases have their own causes. Generally speaking, infectious diseases each have their inherent cause and their medium, such as patients and their utensils, as well as pests such as mosquitoes, flies, fleas, lice, etc., and animals such as rats and dogs. There is also a type of person who does not have symptoms themselves, but can transmit germs to others, and we call this type of person "carriers." In short, the occurrence of diseases all have their individual causes, and infectious diseases have their own transmission routes. At the same time, prevention methods also differ. The transmission routes of infectious diseases can be divided into four categories, which are specifically described as follows:

1. Contact group. The first disease to be mentioned in this group is smallpox. The source of smallpox is an ultrafilterable microorganism. This disease is most easily transmitted by contact with patients. For example, the nasal and oral excretions of patients when they are recovering, toys, and the patient's clothing, etc., can also be the medium of transmission. The second is measles. Measles is the most easily transmitted disease in children. The pathogen of this disease is still not clear, and the transmission route is similar to smallpox. The third is meningitis. This pathogen is a diplococcus, and the transmission route is mostly by direct contact with patients or close contact with carriers. In addition, diseases such as scarlet fever, venereal diseases, skin diseases, and trachoma are all diseases transmitted by contact.

2. Respiratory group. The first disease to be mentioned in this group is diphtheria. The pathogen of diphtheria is a bacillus that invades the throat. It can be transmitted by kissing, shaking hands, and talking with patients or carriers. It is also easy to transmit by touching the patient's food, utensils, chopsticks, and other items. The second is influenza. The pathogen of influenza has not yet been determined, but it spreads rapidly. Among ethnic groups that have not been infected, many die from this disease. During the worldwide influenza pandemic from 1918 to 1919, more than 200 million people were infected, and more than 10 million died. In the United States, in less than half a year, 20 million people were infected, and more than 400,000 died. From June to November 1918, in five months, more than 4 million people in India died from this disease. However, among ethnic groups that have already been infected with this disease, although the infection rate is high, the mortality rate is not high. The transmission route is the same as diphtheria. The next is pneumonia. The pathogen is the pneumonia bacillus. The transmission route is similar to diphtheria and influenza, but overwork, cold, and colds can also induce this disease. In addition, diseases in the contact group can sometimes be transmitted through the respiratory tract.

3. Digestive group. Regarding infectious diseases of the digestive system, there are cholera, typhoid fever, paratyphoid fever, and dysentery. The pathogens of these three diseases are all bacteria, and the transmission routes are almost exactly the same. However, cholera is the most severe, and the mortality rate is very high. I remember that in 1921, there was a cholera pandemic in China. The total number of patients reached more than 150,000, and the number of deaths was more than 50,000. According to statisticians, cholera is expected to have a major epidemic every five years from a statistical point of view. Since there was a major epidemic in 1921, there may still be an epidemic in 1926, which depends on how the prevention work is carried out. The course of typhoid fever and paratyphoid fever is relatively slow, but they are very prevalent in China, and patients can be seen anywhere at any time. In various civilized and advanced countries, due to the perfection of public health facilities, typhoid fever and other diseases have almost disappeared. If there is a case of typhoid fever in the community, medical schools will have the opportunity to practice. Dysentery can be divided into two types, and the nature of the disease is also different. One is bacterial dysentery, which is prevalent in summer and autumn and is easy to treat and prevent. The other is amoebic dysentery, also known as protozoal dysentery. Patients' conditions are sometimes mild and sometimes severe, and it is easy to become a chronic disease, but it is not easy to spread. As for the transmission route, the three diseases are mostly caused by overeating, drinking raw water, and unclean cold foods and drinks, as well as bad environments such as many flies and improper disposal of waste, which can also spread the disease. In addition, most general gastrointestinal diseases originate from dietary habits, which still need to be improved.

4. Inoculation group. There are several infectious diseases that must go through an intermediate host, such as malaria, which must first be bred in the mosquito's body before being transmitted to the human body. There is a very interesting story to be told, that is, when the mosquito that transmits malaria sucks human blood, it must first spit out the liquid in its body before sucking human blood. If the liquid it spits out contains malaria parasites, then the person bitten by the mosquito may develop malaria. The diseases belonging to the parasitic category, such as kala-azar, are mostly caused by white gnats as intermediate hosts. These parasites either enter the skin directly through insect vectors, or are excreted from the body in feces, and then enter the digestive tract through food, directly reaching the internal organs. They then grow and reproduce, either in the intestines, lungs, liver, or blood, to obtain the body's nutrients, destroy tissues, produce toxins, or block ducts, resulting in various physiological disorders. Because this type of disease is infectious, it is also called an infectious disease.

Now that we know how to prevent infectious diseases, we will go a step further. We need to know the sanitary methods of prevention. Now it is divided into two aspects to explain. A. Personal aspects: Infectious diseases are not castles in the air. They all have their transmission factors, and they each have their own vectors when transmitting. Therefore, when it comes to prevention, it should also be explained by category—for infectious diseases in the contact group, the first thing healthy people should do is to separate themselves from patients. This is the "isolation" that the medical community often talks about. When encountering similar patients, they should also not shake hands or talk with them. The second is to implement preventive vaccination, such as vaccinating against smallpox and injecting vaccines against meningitis. For the prevention methods of infectious diseases in the gastrointestinal group, attention should be paid to daily diet. Water should not be drunk unless it has been boiled. At the same time, it must first be known that cold drinks are made from hot water. Attention should be paid to the freshness of food and drink. A good sanitary habit should be developed for diet, and infectious diseases in the gastrointestinal group can be prevented. Preventive injections can also be implemented when necessary. To prevent infectious diseases of the respiratory system, in addition to isolating the patients, it is best to avoid participating in crowded places. As for infectious diseases in the inoculation group, individuals should always pay attention to the cleanliness of the environment. It is best not to use suspicious food. Vectors of infectious diseases such as mosquitoes, flies, lice, fleas, and rats should be eliminated at any time. This can avoid the most common types of infectious diseases. If someone is infected with a certain germ, it sometimes depends on the individual's disease resistance. People who usually pay attention to personal hygiene, have good nutrition, and have suitable living habits have increased resistance, and diseases are not easy to develop. B. Public aspects: We know that the methods of preventing diseases implemented by individuals are relatively easy to implement and effective, but the social environment is too bad, and each individual's environment is different, so the methods of preventing infectious diseases also differ. The first thing to pay attention to is:

1. Environmental improvement. Social environmental sanitation facilities include: Toilet problems—General public toilets should be built with fly-proof screens and doors. At the same time, attention should be paid to management, cleaning, or timely disinfection. In general, unhygienic toilets should be thoroughly guided for improvement, so that toilet construction and management are appropriate and the breeding of flies is reduced. Diet problems—Infectious diseases in the gastrointestinal group are mostly caused by drinking water, so the provision of safe water (tap water) by society is a public health issue. Every summer, Shanghai opens tap water for free use by the general poor, so the number of patients with infectious diseases in the gastrointestinal group has decreased in recent years. This is the most appropriate method of disease prevention, but there are many places without tap water. Ideally, tap water should be installed in various places. The second best option is to find ways to clean the water source, disinfect drinking water, and guide people to develop the habit of drinking boiled water. Problems with the disposal of waste and garbage—The general public still does not know how to pay attention to the disposal of waste and garbage, so society should have responsible agencies or personnel to destroy all waste and garbage to maintain the environmental sanitation of society. Problem of eliminating mosquitoes and flies—Mosquitoes, flies, rats, dogs, etc. are all vectors of infectious diseases, so environmental sanitation facilities should pay attention to eliminating mosquitoes and flies and killing stray dogs and rats at any time and anywhere. There are still many environmental sanitation matters, such as the construction of houses, light transmission and ventilation, and safety equipment in general groups.

2. Medical and pharmaceutical prevention. The prevention work in the medical and pharmaceutical field is to use the principle of artificial immunity to carry out organized and systematic vaccination work according to the season. Vaccination is the same as vaccination and smallpox vaccination. It is now recognized by the world as having special effects, such as smallpox vaccination to prevent smallpox. Injecting typhoid and cholera mixed vaccines can prevent typhoid and cholera. Injecting diphtheria toxoid can prevent diphtheria. All places in society with public health agencies should have this medical and pharmaceutical facility to prevent infectious diseases.

3. Health education. The study of the theory of infectious diseases is a very difficult thing. However, the pathogen and pathology of infectious diseases are very simple, and have already been explained in the previous section. As for prevention methods, personal aspects are certainly not a difficult thing, but only by hoping that the whole society will implement them consistently can this be done. This can only be done by adopting the method of education so that everyone knows the knowledge of infectious diseases and the methods of preventing infectious diseases. This is one of the biggest goals of health education. However, when it comes to health education, there is still the training of applicable health workers to expand the scope of epidemic prevention. The public should also spread the knowledge they have gained.

The above three points have all gone beyond the scope of individual ability. This must be promoted by the government or public groups in order to be effective. Therefore, an issue that arises incidentally is that local governments need to discuss the organization for promoting public health. At present, most local governments have health sections within the Public Security Bureau, which only passively carry out some medical and pharmaceutical crackdown work, which cannot meet the needs of today's society. Provincial health experiment offices are being established in various provinces one after another, health bureaus are being established in various cities, and health centers or county hospitals are being established in various counties, but many provinces, cities, and counties have still failed to promote public health work in an organized manner. This is the most important prerequisite for preventing infectious diseases.

Treatment: There are already special treatments for infectious diseases, such as quinine for treating malaria, organic arsenic drugs such as compound 914 for treating syphilis, and santonin for treating roundworms. This is already known to everyone. The treatment of other diseases, such as diphtheria antitoxin treatment, is often complicated and cannot be explained in a short time, so I will not introduce it for the time being. However, there are several diseases for which there is still no special medicine that can be treated scientifically, but by starting from the aspect of caring for the patient's life, the condition can gradually improve until recovery. For example, for typhoid fever, as long as the patient's diet is controlled and the patient is completely bedridden, this is a method of nursing care that temporarily replaces treatment. There is also measles, which also has no special medicine that can be treated. Only by using nursing methods to maintain a balanced temperature in the patient's room and prevent other complications can the patient naturally recover within a considerable amount of time. In addition, there are many types of infectious diseases in which the treatment may still be awaiting the invention of drugs, or even the use of diet and nutrition instead of treatment. This is exactly the situation of modern medical evolution.

Conclusion: We know that there are very few special medicines for the treatment of infectious diseases. At the same time, due to the poor social environment, there are very many opportunities for the spread of infectious diseases. If you wait until you are sick before seeking medical treatment, the time and economic costs are not appropriate. What's more, the distribution of the number of doctors in our country is also impossible. Therefore, if we want to talk about the health of the nation today, the work of preventing infectious diseases is probably thousands of times better than the treatment of diseases! The work of preventing diseases is more important than treatment, but the work of preventing diseases must be carried out in cooperation between the government and the people. The people must earnestly implement a healthy life, and the government should also strive to build health. Only then can human life gradually progress and social civilization can be renewed day by day. (The End)

New Subsidiary Coins Approved for Issuance on the 10th 95

The Number Minted Has Been Handed Over to the Central Bank for Exclusive Issuance. Chen Jian'an Has Gone to Beijing to Report to Minister Kong.

According to the New Voice Agency, after the Central Mint was ordered to mint subsidiary coins, the minted copper half-cent and one-cent coins and the nickel five-cent, ten-cent, and twenty-cent coins, totaling five types of subsidiary coins, have been reviewed and found to be in compliance with the subsidiary coin regulations. They have been packed and sent to the Central Bank in preparation for issuance and circulation on the market starting from the 10th. The Ministry of Finance's announcement is recorded as follows: It is hereby announced that the subsidiary coin regulations have been promulgated and implemented by the National Government, and the Ministry has ordered the Central Mint to actively mint the coins. These subsidiary coins have now been minted and stored in large quantities, and should be issued urgently for circulation. It is hereby stipulated that the 10th of this month shall be the date of issuance of subsidiary coins. In addition to submitting a report to the Executive Yuan for transmission to the National Government for the record and distributing it to various places, this announcement is hereby issued for public knowledge.

Chen Jian'an, Vice President of the Central Bank and Director of the Central Mint, went to Beijing from Shanghai the night before last to report to Minister of Finance Kong Xiangxi on the minting of subsidiary coins. Review Standing Committee: Amendment to Regulations 97

The Central Mint Review Committee held a regular meeting at 4:30 PM on the 14th of this month in the conference room on the third floor of the Central Bank. The meeting included reports on committee affairs. It was noted that Articles 7 and 9 of the committee's regulations originally only stipulated reviews of new coins minted by the Central Mint and ingots, excluding subsidiary coinage. Now, a decision has been made to amend the regulations to include provisions regarding the fineness and weight of subsidiary coinage.

The Value of Twenty-Cent Coins Collapses: Each Yuan Rises to 12.20 Cents, Hoarders Dumping Double Dimes for Legal Tender

According to the Huadong News Agency, on November 4th of last year, the Ministry of Finance stipulated exchange rates: one yuan of legal tender could be exchanged for twelve cents in small foreign coins, five hundred wen for double dimes, and three thousand wen for copper coins. At one point, some people in the market were buying up twenty-cent coins, causing the premium to rise sharply. The black market price for double dimes reached a high of eleven cents and one fen. Recently, twenty-cent coins have been circulating with excellent credit, and the market demand for double dimes has decreased daily. Those who hoarded them also felt the pain of not generating interest, and merchants who had hoarded them could no longer manipulate the market. As a result, they successively released their holdings, leading to an oversupply of twenty-cent coins. Yesterday, the silver market quoted a premium of seven fen, single dimes at 833.33 yuan per 1000, double dimes at 833.33 yuan per 1000, an exchange rate of 1200 cents, copper coins at 300,000 per unit, blank coin at 350 wen, a premium of 50 wen, and a black market price of 12.23 cents for double dimes. Exchange shops were exchanging at a rate of 12.20 cents, while double dimes were only trading between 480 to 490 wen. There was a surplus on all sides. This reporter inquired with the financial community, and it was said that the reason for this was that the Ministry of Finance had minted new subsidiary coins. Manipulators initially believed that the authorities would immediately buy them up, so they hoarded them. However, the market did not need these silver subsidiary coins, and the authorities did not immediately abolish or melt them down, leading to an oversupply. Those who hoarded them not only failed to profit but suffered losses and had to dump them. Previously, the tram company took in more than 20,000 yuan in double dimes daily, but now, because twenty-cent notes can be exchanged for legal tender without loss, passengers prefer to use twenty-cent coins and disregard double dimes. The daily intake of double dimes has dropped to only 7,000 or 8,000 yuan, indirectly affecting those who hoard double dimes, causing the price of double dimes to shrink. With the imminent circulation of new subsidiary coins, citizens should be happy to use the new coins and avoid exchanging them for miscellaneous coins, which would lead to losses from exchange fees. This proves that after the implementation of the new subsidiary coins, all abnormal conditions will naturally be eliminated, and the people will no longer be subject to exploitation and loss in their daily use.

German Goodwill Visit Ship Will Head Straight to Japan, Bypassing China, German Community's Telegram Protesting Ship Visiting Shanghai Unsuccessful, Captain Siemens Carries 600 Officers and Soldiers 102

According to the Xinsheng News Agency, the cruiser "Karlsruhe," dispatched by the German government for goodwill visits to various countries, arrived in Hong Kong yesterday morning after passing through Batavia and the Philippines. According to news received from semi-official German sources in Shanghai, the ship will stay in Hong Kong for ten days and then head directly to Japan without passing through Shanghai. It is also scheduled to visit the United States via the Aleutian Islands before returning to Germany after a ten-day stay in Japan. Six years ago, the German parliament sent the Emden warship to visit China, staying in both Beijing and Shanghai for a long time. Three years ago, the Köln warship was sent to Shanghai and Qingdao. At a time when rumors of a military alliance between Japan and Germany are rife, the German community is quite suspicious that the ship will head directly to Japan without passing through China. It is rumored that the German community in Shanghai telegraphed in advance to protest, hoping that it would visit Shanghai, but it was ineffective, which greatly dissatisfied the German community. It is also learned that the ship's captain is Mr. Siemens, and it carries 600 officers and soldiers. The ship was built in 1927, has a displacement of 6,000 tons, is 186 yards long, and 17 yards wide, with a speed of 32 knots per hour. It is armed with nine 15-centimeter guns, four 8.8-centimeter anti-aircraft guns, eight 3.7-centimeter guns, and twelve No. 50 submarines. Because Germany is restricted by the Treaty of Versailles from building warships over 6,000 tons, the "Karlsruhe" is currently the largest warship in Germany.

Sino-Japanese Wireless Telephone Communication, Subsequent Types Announced, Communication Divided into Calling a Person, Calling a Number, and Call Transfer, Chinese Area Connect to No. 40, Concession Area No. 03

According to the International Telecommunications Bureau's announcement yesterday, Shanghai-Tokyo international wireless telephone service will be open for commercial use from the 15th of this month. The types of calls, fees, and procedures have been completely determined. The details are as follows: Types of calls: (A) Call Person (must first state your name and telephone number, and specify the telephone number and person to be called), (B) Call Number (refers to calls where the name of the person being called or calling is not specified, only the telephone number is specified), (C) Call Transfer (calls to a specific person at a specific location where the other party does not have a telephone and must be notified by the exchange). Fees: The initial three minutes are priced at 15 yuan in legal tender. Calls shorter than three minutes are still charged for three minutes. For each additional minute or part thereof, an additional 5 yuan in legal tender will be charged (all three types of calls are priced the same). Procedures: To call from the Chinese area of the city, first connect to No. 40. To call from the concession area, first connect to No. 03, then request registration. Then declare the type of call you want to make. After the international call is connected, the exchange will notify you to speak. For inquiries about international calls, you can dial 41000 (Chinese area) or 02 (concession area) and transfer to 41000. Cancellation Fee: If the other party does not want to talk after the international call has been connected, or the person being called cannot be found, it will be treated as a cancellation, and a cancellation fee of 1.50 yuan in legal tender must be paid.

According to the Central News Agency, Mr. Arima Aki, the first Japanese Ambassador to China, who was recalled to his country, departed from Shanghai with his wife and staff last night at midnight on the Japanese ship Chichibu Maru. He is scheduled to arrive in Shanghai on the afternoon of the 26th. The details are as follows:

Embarked on Ship Last Night 108

Ambassador Arima, who is 62 years old, came to China on September 4, 1932, which was after the September 18th and January 28th Incidents. He has been in office for three years, five months, and three days. After receiving the order from his government to be transferred, Arima went to Nanjing to bid farewell to the central authorities of China, and then held a tea party in Shanghai to bid farewell to leaders from all walks of life in China and abroad. Farewell by Various Circles 109

Yesterday evening, snowflakes were falling, and leaders from various circles in China and Japan braved the snow to see him off at the Huishan Wharf, including the new Chinese Ambassador to Japan, Xu Shiying, Ambassador to France, Wei Jun, Mayor of Shanghai, Wu Tiecheng, Director of the Shanghai Office of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Zhou Jue, and Commissioner of the Municipal Government, Wang Changchun. Ambassador Arima shook hands with each person who came to see him off in the ship's hall, and refreshments were served to express his gratitude. Around 11:00 PM, those who came to see him off began to leave the ship one after another.

Ambassador Arima shared his thoughts at 11:00 PM last night in the Chichibu Maru's meeting room, meeting with Chinese and Japanese journalists and saying, "I was ordered to serve as ambassador to China, and it has suddenly been three and a half years. During my tenure, I have had very harmonious relations with the government and people of your country, which is a great honor. As I leave office, I am grateful for the farewells from leaders from all walks of life in your country, and I am even more grateful for those who braved the snow to come and see me off tonight. As for Sino-Japanese relations, I firmly believe that China and Japan are brotherly nations, and should embrace the determination to coexist and prosper together, and strive for common existence in the world. Although temporary misunderstandings between the two countries cannot be avoided at present, I firmly believe that they will soon become more friendly. Today, as I am ordered to leave China and return home, these are my thoughts on the Sino-Japanese issue."

Page 11

Ministry of Finance Cables Provincial, Municipal, and County Governments: Receipts Should Be Given for Confiscated Silver Coins 117

After seizure, should be handed over to the bureau to be forwarded to the court for disposal; those who confiscate directly will be charged with intent to embezzle

According to the Xinxin News Agency, the Ministry of Finance has stated that if public security bureau officers and police seize smuggled silver coins and silver items, the person and the silver should be sent to the local public security bureau for interrogation. If confiscation is warranted, a receipt should be issued immediately. Officers and police should not confiscate directly to prevent abuse. The Ministry of Finance has sent a cable to the provincial, municipal, and county governments to instruct all relevant agencies to investigate. The original cable from the Ministry of Finance is recorded below: It has recently been reported that public security bureau officers and police in various provinces and cities confiscate smuggled silver coins and silver items without issuing receipts, which has led to abuse. Please instruct them to correct this. In cases where public security officers and police seize smuggled silver coins and silver items, they should be handed over to the local public security bureau for processing. If there is concealment or intent to evade taxes, the public security authorities should forward them to the court for prosecution in accordance with the Emergency Law for Punishing Acts Endangering the Republic of China. However, for silver coins and silver items directly confiscated by the public security bureau, a receipt should be issued as evidence. In the future, in cases where officers and police seize smuggled silver coins and silver items, the person and the silver should be sent to the public security bureau for interrogation. If confiscation is warranted, a receipt should be issued immediately. Officers and police should not confiscate directly, and violators will be charged with intent to embezzle, in order to prevent abuse. In addition to sending a separate cable, this cable is for investigation, and you are requested to instruct the affiliated public security bureaus to comply.

New Locomotive of the Jiangnan Railway Company Has Been Transported to Nanjing 119

Polish engineer accompanies to be responsible for installation and testing

The Jiangnan Railway Company ordered a large locomotive from the Polish Poznan Jelski Company last year. The company shipped it last winter on the Blackby Forde, from the port of Gdansk, Poland, to Shanghai. It arrived in port on January 20, unloaded at Wusong, and the company specially sent engineer Okinsek and mechanic Lonecki with the ship to China, responsible for unloading and testing. The tests in Shanghai were very satisfactory. It was transported to Nanjing by the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway the day before yesterday, and representatives from the Jiangnan Company and the Polish engineer and mechanic also went. According to Polish engineer Okinsek, Poland's heavy industry has developed extraordinarily in recent years, and its production of various machinery, armaments, airplanes, etc. is very high, especially railway materials such as railway bridges, locomotives, passenger cars, etc. The prices are very low, and they are strong and durable. Many countries such as the Soviet Union, Romania, Turkey, and other European countries order from Poland. The Songhua River Railway Bridge in Harbin, China, was built by the Warsaw Lotzky Company of Poland. This is the first time that China has ordered locomotives on a trial basis, and it is hoped that various routes will be able to purchase and use them in the future. He also said that Polish railways already use streamlined locomotives and passenger cars, but because the speed is very high, heavier tracks must be used.

International Trade Bureau Announces Last Year's International Trade Trends 120

According to the New Sound News Agency, the International Trade Bureau announced the trends in China's international trade last year, stating that although foreign trade in the 24th year of the Republic of China still showed signs of contraction in terms of total value, an analysis of imports and exports revealed that exports increased by 7% compared to the previous year due to the stimulus of low silver prices. Conversely, import trade decreased by 10% compared to the previous year due to the increase in tariff prices and a subsequent decline in the import of foreign goods. Generally speaking, foreign trade in the 24th year of the Republic of China had already shown signs of improvement. In terms of import and export commodities, tung oil was the most important export commodity, valued at over 41.58 million yuan. Silk was second, valued at over 40.23 million yuan. Eggs and egg products were third, valued at 32.06 million yuan. Metals and metal products were fourth, valued at 31.67 million yuan. In addition, tea, tanned hides and leather goods, and cotton were each valued at over 20 million yuan. Peanut cotton yarn, grains and products, wool, drawn thread, ramie, and pig bristles also had export values of over 15 million yuan. Compared to the previous year, most commodities increased, with tung oil increasing by 59%. The main market remained the United States, accounting for 70% of total exports. Exports to Hong Kong, the United Kingdom, France, and the Netherlands also increased compared to the previous year. Silk exports also increased by over 41% compared to the previous year. However, in terms of silk categories, apart from white silk, which increased by over 13 million yuan, other types such as dougong silk, grey silk, and waste silk also increased, but only slightly. Yellow silk tended to decline, by about one-sixth. The United States was the largest overseas market, valued at over 13.7 million yuan, with white silk accounting for the majority. Annual sales exceeded three times that of the previous year. France was second to the United States, valued at over 12.53 million yuan, also with white silk accounting for the majority. Sales last year exceeded twice that of the previous year. In addition, India remained a market for Chinese silk, valued at 4.08 million yuan, with yellow silk accounting for almost all of it. However, the sales value was lower than the previous year. The export situation for eggs and egg products was good last year, increasing by 6% compared to the previous year. The United Kingdom remained the largest market, valued at over 18.46 million yuan. The United States was second, valued at 4.62 million yuan. Germany was third, valued at 2.84 million yuan. In addition, exports to Hong Kong, the Netherlands, and other places each reached over 1 million yuan. Compared to the previous year, there was no increase or decrease in the United Kingdom, a slight increase in Germany and France, and brisk sales in the United States. Metal and metal products also increased in exports last year compared to the previous year. Tin ingots and antimony accounted for the majority, with more than two-thirds being shipped to Hong Kong, valued at 19.98 million yuan. Among other commodities, only tea saw a decline in sales in the United Kingdom and Russia. Exports last year decreased by 16% compared to the previous year. Fortunately, sales in Morocco were brisk, otherwise the decline would have been even greater. The decline in cotton yarn was even more severe, decreasing by 39% compared to the previous year. Exports to Japan and Korea last year were only one-third of the previous year. Exports of hides and leather goods also decreased by 16%. Goat skin and lambskin saw the most significant decline. The United States remained the largest export market, but sales in both Europe and the United States declined. Silk exports also declined, decreasing by 31% compared to the previous year. Sales in Hong Kong, India, and the United Kingdom all declined. The failure of silk last year can be seen here. As for cotton, peanuts, and sesame, exports all increased sharply last year. Wool, pig bristles, grains, and other items all saw slight increases. Overall, the prosperity of native product exports last year was a rare phenomenon in recent years. As for major import commodities, rice once again ranked first last year, valued at 50.9 million gold units, an increase of 52% compared to the previous year. The majority of imported rice came from Annam, valued at 28.85 million gold units. In addition, large amounts were imported from Siam and India. Copper and iron were second, valued at 40.39 million gold units, a decrease of 9% compared to the previous year. The main sources remained Germany and the United Kingdom, each reaching 8 to 9 million gold units. In addition, imports from the United States and Japan each reached over 5 million gold units. Machinery (including machine tools) ranked third, valued at 35.41 million gold units, an increase of 17% compared to the previous year. Electrical machinery and other unnamed machinery saw the most significant increase. As for textile machinery, there was no increase or decrease. Engine machinery, on the other hand, declined. The majority of imported machinery came from Germany, valued at 8.94 million gold units. Imports from the United Kingdom and Japan were also over 7 million gold units each. Imports from the United States were valued at 5.3 million gold units. Cotton ranked fourth, valued at 22.78 million gold units, a sharp decrease of half compared to the previous year. The majority still came from the United States, valued at 12.97 million gold units. Imports from India were second, valued at over 6 million gold units. Rubber ranked fifth, valued at 20.94 million gold units, an increase of 20% compared to the previous year. The majority came from the United States, followed by Italy, France, and Canada. Kerosene ranked sixth, valued at 20.57 million gold units, an increase of only 1% compared to the previous year. The majority still came from the United States, valued at over 9 million gold units. The Dutch East Indies was second, valued at 8.24 million gold units. Imports from Russia were valued at just over 2 million gold units. Other commodities, in order, were dyes, pigments, chemical products, and pharmaceuticals, each valued at over 20 million gold units. Wheat and timber were each valued at over 19 million gold units. Metal products were valued at 18.83 million gold units. Vehicles and sugar were each valued at over 15 million gold units. Cotton cloth was valued at over 11 million gold units. Wool and wool fabrics, gasoline, and diesel were each valued at over 10 million gold units. In addition, the import value of other foreign goods was less than 10 million gold units. In summary, the import value of major foreign goods generally decreased last year compared to the previous year. The low silver price, the increase in tariff prices, and the weak domestic purchasing power were also major reasons. Only machinery, paper, timber, dyes, pigments, and gasoline saw slight increases, but the amount was minimal. The imports of both rice and wheat increased significantly compared to the previous year, despite the decline in imports. The former increased by 52%, while the latter increased by 22%, which is a deep concern for the livelihood of our people.

The Shanghai Overseas Chinese Affairs Bureau, in order to facilitate the return of overseas Chinese, previously established an inquiry office in the Jianghai Customs Building. Copper Mine Source Discovered in Huangshigang 126

Shanghai Electrical Manufacturing Industry Association Sends Letters to Sichuan and Yunnan Provinces Inquiring About Mining Details

According to the New News Agency, the Shanghai Electrical Manufacturing Industry Association believes that copper is a necessary raw material for the industry. A mine source has now been found near Huangshigang.
